Jinling Yangjia Wonton Restaurant ‚Äì ÈáëÈôµÊù®ÂÆ∂È¶ÑÈ•®Â∫ó\\nFamous for its delicious wontons, Jinling Yangjia Wonton Restaurant is highly rated by customers, with its Duck Blood Wontons being a standout specialty unique to Nanjing.\\nThe restaurant‚Äôs open kitchen lets customers observe the whole process, from making pork lard to preparing and cooking the wontons. The pork lard and chili oil are both homemade, adding to the authenticity.\\nThe wontons arrive in a fragrant golden broth, topped with pepper and finely chopped greens. Each wonton is generously filled and wrapped in a delicate, thin skin. The tender, bouncy duck blood adds a delightful texture, while the broth is rich and flavorful. A dash of homemade chili oil brings out even more savory goodness, making it irresistibly appetizing.\\nThe duck blood is served separately, and for those who like spice, a bit more chili oil enhances the aroma and taste even further.\\nüìçAddress: 1-1 Caodu Xiang, Baixia District\\n14. Xiaopanji Duck Blood Vermicelli Soup ‚Äì Â∞èÊΩòËÆ∞È∏≠Ë°ÄÁ≤â‰∏ùÊ±§\\nAt first glance, Xiaopanji may appear ordinary, but once inside, the long line tells a different story. Customers often wait about ten minutes for their bowl of duck blood vermicelli soup, a sign of its popularity.\\nXiaopanji‚Äôs duck blood vermicelli soup is known for its rich, flavorful broth, using thin vermicelli noodles paired with duck blood, tofu, and more. Each spoonful is packed with ingredients, making it a savory delight that leaves a lasting impression.\\nThe special duck blood vermicelli soup stands out with its extra toppings, including crispy rice crackers and large braised eggs, adding even more layers of flavor.\\nFor those who find the special version too loaded or dislike certain ingredients, Xiaopanji also offers alternatives like duck leg vermicelli soup and duck breast vermicelli soup, both of which are equally tasty.\\nüìçAddress: 2 Jiangjun Ln, Xuanwu District\\n15. Gaoyou Noodle Restaurant ‚Äì È´òÈÇÆÈù¢È¶Ü\\nHidden in the quiet Lujiagang Alley behind the busy New Street area, Gaoyou Noodle Restaurant can be tricky to find, and you might need a local to guide you. Despite its out-of-the-way location, the restaurant‚Äôs famous dry mixed noodles with green pepper, tofu, and shredded pork have earned it a solid reputation.\\nA large, aromatic bowl of noodles is served, with stir-fried toppings coating the noodles in rich flavor. Generous portions of tofu and juicy shredded pork make it a dish that invites immediate enjoyment.\\nThe thin Gaoyou noodles are soaked in sauce, and after mixing the noodles and toppings, the flavor becomes even more intense.\\nThe secret to these noodles is the black pepper from Sichuan, which clings to each noodle strand and adds a robust, flavorful kick.\\nüìçAddress: 1 Lujia Ln, Qinhuai District\\nüå∏Final Thoughts: Where to Eat in Nanjing\\nTo wrap things up, Nanjing‚Äôs food scene is full of incredible flavors, and these 15 restaurants offer some of the best dining experiences in the city. ‚Äî 11+ best Nanjing street food & Nanjing famous food you must try\\nBy\\nNikki Dang\\n-\\nOctober 6, 2023\\n\\nNanjing, located in Jiangsu province, China, is a city with a rich history and cultural significance. It was the capital of several Chinese dynasties and served as the capital of the Republic of China in the early 20th century. Nanjing is known for its historical sites, beautiful landscapes, and, of course, its culinary specialties. So, what to eat in Nanjing? Let‚Äôs check out our suggested 11+ best food in Nanjing, Nanjing famous food and Nanjing street food you must try when coming to this beautiful ancient city!\\n\\nWhat to eat in Chengdu? ‚Äî 19+ must-try, famous food & best Chengdu street food to eat\\nWhat to eat in Shanghai? ‚Äî 17+ most popular, must eat & best street food in Shanghai\\nWhere to go in Shanghai at night? 25+ must-visit & best places to visit in Shanghai at night\\nWhat to do in Shanghai at night? 21+ top activities & best things to do in Shanghai at night\\n9+ most beautiful & best ancient towns in China\\n\\n \\nNanjing skyline\\n\\nA view of Nanjing Fuzimiao\\n\\nA busy street at Fuzimiao | nanjing street food\\n\\nNanjing street food | nanjing street food\\n\\n| nanjing street food\\nNanjing cuisine is one of the most influential and interesting features of China. Most visitors find the local delicacies here irresistible. Famous for its delicate preparation and rich flavors, each dish has its own charm. Now, let‚Äôs explore the best food of Nanjing and try it on your next visit to the ‚ÄúCapital of Six Dynasties‚Äù of China.\\n\\nNanjing typical food | nanjing street food\\nSalted Duck (top nanjing street food)\\nOne of Nanjing‚Äôs most beloved dishes is Nanjing salted duck. It is a traditional dish that has been enjoyed for centuries and holds a significant place in the local cuisine. It is a must-try specialty for food enthusiasts visiting the city, offering a unique and flavorful experience.\\n\\nNanjing salted duck | nanjing street food\\nThe preparation of Nanjing Salted Duck involves marinating the duck with a mixture of salt, spices, and other seasonings before air-drying or brining it. Nanjing salted duck has a unique flavor profile. The meat is savory, with a hint of sweetness and a delicate saltiness from the curing process. The skin is thin and crispy, offering a delightful contrast in texture to the tender meat.\\n\\nTexture of salted duck | nanjing street food\\nNanjing salted duck is typically served sliced, either as a standalone dish or as part of a larger meal. It is often accompanied by condiments like soy sauce, hoisin sauce, scallions, and cucumbers. The slices of salted duck can be wrapped in thin pancakes or enjoyed with steamed buns, allowing diners to create their own flavorful combinations.\\n\\nNanjing salted duck is typically served sliced | nanjing street food\\nWhere to try salted duck in Nanjing? (nanjing famous food)\\nWhen it comes to enjoying Nanjing salted duck, there are several popular addresses in Nanjing where you can savor this local delicacy. Here are a few renowned places:\\nNanjing Impressions: Hunan Walking Street, No.2 Shiziqiao Hunan Road. They serve authentic salted duck along with other local specialties in a nostalgic and culturally rich atmosphere.\\n\\nAt Nanjing Impressions | nanjing street food\\nLocal Street Food Stalls: In addition to restaurants, you can find street food stalls and local markets in Nanjing where vendors sell salted duck and other local delicacies. These stalls offer a more casual and authentic dining experience, allowing you to immerse yourself in the local food culture.\\n\\nA food stall selling salted ducks and roast ducks, @Visit Jiangsu FB | nanjing street food\\nJinling Roast Duck (what to eat in nanjing)\\nJinling roast duck is a famous variation of roast duck that originated in Nanjing. It is named after Nanjing‚Äôs historical moniker, ‚ÄúJinling,‚Äù which means ‚Äúcapital of Jin.‚Äù Although Jinling roast duck is not as famous around the world as Pecking roast duck in Beijing, its taste and scrumptiousness are just as exceptional.\\n\\nJinling roast duck | nanjing street food\\nSimilar to other roast duck dishes, Jinling roast duck involves a meticulous preparation process. The duck is first cleaned and dressed, and then it is marinated with a combination of various seasonings and spices. The marinade typically includes soy sauce, ginger, garlic, sugar, and other aromatic ingredients. The duck is left to absorb the flavors for a specific period, ensuring a rich and well-seasoned taste.\\n\\nRoasted in a closed oven | nanjing street food\\nAfter the preparation process, the duck is traditionally roasted in a closed oven using fruit tree wood as fuel. This roasting technique helps impart a distinctive smoky aroma and a beautiful golden-brown color to the duck. The slow and controlled roasting process ensures that the meat remains tender and succulent while the skin becomes crispy.\\n\\nJinling roast ducks ready on hooks | nanjing street food\\nWhen the roast duck is ready to serve, the meat is tender and juicy, infused with the aromatic blend of spices from the marinade. The skin is thin and crispy, providing a delightful contrast in texture. The combination of the savory meat and the flavorful skin creates a harmonious and satisfying taste.\\n\\nTender and juicy texture, @Maggie-Hiufu-Wong/CNN | nanjing street food\\nJinling roast duck is typically served sliced, accompanied by thin pancakes or steamed buns. The slices of duck are traditionally enjoyed by wrapping them in pancakes along with condiments like hoisin sauce, cucumber, scallions, and sometimes sugar or garlic paste.\\n\\nA good pair\\nWhere to try salted duck in Nanjing? (best food in nanjing)\\nNanjing Impressions: Hunan Walking Street, No.2 Shiziqiao Hunan Road, Nanjing.\\nNanjing Deji Plaza: 18 Zhongshan Rd, Xuanwu District, Nanjing. Deji Plaza is a popular shopping and dining complex in Nanjing. It houses several restaurants that serve Jinling roast duck, allowing you to savor this local specialty while exploring the vibrant city center.\\n\\nAnother way to enjoy Jinling roast duck is in thin slices | nanjing street food\\nFuzimiao (Confucius Temple) area and Shiziqiao Food Street, can also lead you to hidden gems and smaller establishments where you can indulge in authentic Jinling roast duck.\\n\\nShiziqiao Food Street | nanjing street food\\nDuck Blood Vermicelli Soup\\nDuck blood vermicelli soup, also known as ‚ÄúYa Xue Fen Si Tang‚Äù in Chinese, is a popular dish in Nanjing cuisine. The name of this dish sounds strange and you will surely be very curious, wondering how blood and soup are combined.\\n\\nDuck blood vermicelli soup | nanjing street food\\nThe soup is prepared by simmering the ingredients together in a flavorful broth. The duck blood curd is sliced and added to the soup, where it absorbs the flavors of the broth. The vermicelli noodles, duck meat, tofu, mushrooms, and other ingredients are also cooked in the broth until they are tender and infused with the soup‚Äôs flavors.\\n\\nA portion served in a small clay pot | nanjing street food\\nDuck blood vermicelli soup has a rich and savory flavor. The broth is usually seasoned with ingredients like soy sauce, ginger, garlic, and sometimes chili or other spices to add a touch of heat. The duck blood curd has a unique gelatinous texture and a mild, slightly metallic taste that blends well with the other ingredients in the soup.\\n\\nA flavorful bowl of duck blood vermicelli soup | nanjing street food\\nIt is typically served hot in a bowl and often garnished with chopped scallions or cilantro for added freshness and flavor.¬†You can find duck blood vermicelli soup easily in Nanjing, especially at food stalls in Fuzimiao food street for only 0.5 USD. You should try this delicious dish.\\nEgg Shaomai\\nEgg shaomai, also known as ‚ÄúDan Zi Shao Mai‚Äù in Chinese, is a popular street food and dim sum dish in Nanjing. It is primarily made with a combination of eggs, ground pork, shrimp, mushrooms, and other seasonings. The filling is typically mixed together and wrapped in a thin, delicate dumpling wrapper. It is a must-try when exploring the local food scene in Nanjing.\\n\\nEgg shaomai | nanjing famous food\\nThe preparation process for egg shaomai involves several steps. The filling ingredients are finely chopped or minced and mixed together with seasonings like soy sauce, ginger, garlic, and sometimes sesame oil or other spices. The mixture is then spooned onto a dumpling wrapper, folded into a pleated shape, and topped with a small piece of shrimp.\\nOnce assembled, the egg shaomai are traditionally steamed in bamboo steamers, allowing them to cook gently and retain their moisture. The steaming process ensures that the dumpling wrappers become soft and translucent while the filling is cooked to perfection.\\n\\nAnother look of egg shaomai | nanjing famous food\\nEgg shaomai has a delightful combination of flavors. The filling is savory and rich, with the umami taste of the pork and shrimp complemented by the earthiness of mushrooms and the aroma of seasonings. The addition of the egg provides a silky and creamy texture to the filling, enhancing its overall taste.\\n\\nEgg shaomai at Halal Ma Xiangxing restaurant | nanjing famous food\\nEgg shaomai is typically served in bamboo steamers, with each steamer holding several pieces of shaomai. It is often enjoyed as a snack or as part of a dim sum meal. The shaomai can be eaten on their own or dipped in condiments such as soy sauce, chili oil, or a combination of sauces for added flavor.\\nWonderful egg shaomai at Halal Ma Xiangxing restaurant is recommended ‚Äì where the dish was invented for a Chinese general who loved shaomai and shrimp. Here, they use fresh shrimp made into a paste and wrapped in a thin egg-based dumpling. Address: No.32, Yunnan North Road, Gulou District, Nanjing; open daily from 6:30 a.m. to 8:30 p.m.\\n\\n| nanjing famous food\\nTangbao (soup dumplings)\\nTangbao, also known as soup dumplings, is a type of dumpling filled with a flavorful broth and a mixture of meat and/or vegetables. They are known for their delicate and thin dumpling wrappers, which contain a hot, savory soup inside.\\n\\nTangbao (soup dumplings) | nanjing famous food\\nThe filling of Tangbao typically consists of minced pork, shrimp, crab meat, or a combination of these ingredients. Other variations may include vegetables such as bamboo shoots or mushrooms. The broth is made by simmering meat or bones, along with aromatic spices and seasonings, to create a flavorful and gelatinous soup.\\n\\nInviting tangbao | nanjing famous food\\nTangbao are traditionally steamed in bamboo steamers, which allows the dumplings to cook gently and retain their shape and juiciness. The steaming process activates the gelatin in the broth, transforming it into a hot, savory soup that is locked inside the dumpling.\\n\\nTangbao served in a bamboo steamer | nanjing street food\\nEnjoying Tangbao is a unique experience. The dumplings are typically served in bamboo steamers or small plates. To eat them, you can use chopsticks to carefully lift a Tangbao from the steamer, taking care not to puncture the delicate wrapper. You can then place the dumpling on a spoon and take a small bite from the corner to release the hot soup. Be cautious as the broth may be hot. You can then savor the combination of the flavorful soup and the filling. You will definitely fall in love with this adorable snack!\\n\\nWhat a delicious look! | nanjing famous food\\nTangbao are often served with a dipping sauce made from a combination of soy sauce, vinegar, and sometimes ginger or chili oil. This sauce adds an extra layer of tanginess and enhances the overall flavor of the dumplings.\\n\\nTangbao served with a dipping sauce | nanjing famous food\\nNanjing is known for its rich Tangbao culture, and there are numerous restaurants and street food stalls throughout the city that specialize in this dish. Some recommended places for you are:\\nYinshi Jishi Tangbao: No. 398 Mochou Road, Baixia District, Nanjing. They‚Äôre open every day from 6:30 a.m. to 7:30 p.m, and it costs about 1.8 USD for eight small bite-sized pieces of Tangbao.\\nFuzimiao (Confucius Temple) and Hunan Road are particularly renowned for their Tangbao offerings.\\nPan-fried Beef Dumplings\\nPan-fried beef dumplings, also known as ‚ÄúGuo Tie‚Äù or ‚ÄúJian Jiao‚Äù in Chinese, are a popular street food and snack in Nanjing. Pan-fried beef dumplings are a type of dumplings made with a thin wheat-based wrapper filled with a savory mixture of ground beef and seasonings. They are pan-fried until crispy on the bottom while maintaining a tender and juicy filling.\\n\\nPan-fried beef dumplings | nanjing famous food\\nThe filling for pan-fried beef dumplings typically consists of minced or ground beef combined with aromatics such as ginger, garlic, and green onions. Additional seasonings may include soy sauce, sesame oil, and sometimes spices like Sichuan peppercorns for a hint of heat.\\n\\nA tender and juicy filling | what to eat in nanjing\\nThe dumplings are cooked in a hot, oiled skillet or pan. They are first placed flat-side down and allowed to cook until the bottom becomes golden and crispy. Water is then added to the pan, and the dumplings are covered to steam. This steaming process helps to cook the filling thoroughly and ensure it remains juicy and tender. Once the water has evaporated, the dumplings continue to fry until the bottom becomes crispy again.\\n\\nThe dumplings are cooked in a hot, oiled skillet or pan. | what to eat in nanjing\\nPan-fried beef dumplings are typically served with a dipping sauce that adds an extra layer of flavor. Common dipping sauces include soy sauce, vinegar, and sometimes chili oil or sesame oil. Some people also enjoy adding minced garlic or ginger to the dipping sauce for additional zing.\\n\\n| what to eat in nanjing\\nWhere to try Pan-fried beef dumplings? (nanjing street food)\\nLiji Halal restaurant: No. 1, Dading Xiang, Pingshi Jie, Baixia District, Nanjing. The restaurant is open from 5:30 a.m. to 7:30 p.m. at a cost of around 0.7 USD for five pieces.\\n\\nLiji Halal Restaurant | what to eat in nanjing\\nPan-fried beef dumplings can also be found in various street food stalls, local eateries throughout Nanjing. They are often freshly made to order, ensuring their crispiness and deliciousness.\\nStinky Tofu\\nStinky tofu, also known as ‚ÄúChou Dou Fu‚Äù in Chinese, is a unique and polarizing street food in Nanjing. Whether you love stinky tofu or find it challenging, it is an intriguing culinary experience that represents the bold and diverse food culture of Nanjing.\\n\\nStinky tofu street food | what to eat in nanjing\\nThe process of making stinky tofu involves several steps. First, fresh tofu is soaked in brine made with various ingredients like fermented vegetables, dried shrimp, and spices. The tofu is then left to ferment for a period of time, from a few days to several weeks, depending on the desired intensity of flavor. After fermentation, the tofu is typically deep-fried until it develops a crispy golden exterior.\\n\\nStinky tofu cubes with crispy golden exterior | what to eat in nanjing\\nStinky tofu has a strong and pungent smell, which some describe as resembling rotten garbage or cheese. However, despite its odor, the taste of stinky tofu is often milder and more savory. The fermentation process gives the tofu a unique and complex flavor, with hints of umami and a slightly sour or tangy note.\\n\\n| what to eat in nanjing\\nStinky tofu is commonly served as a street food snack in Nanjing. It is often cut into bite-sized pieces and skewered on bamboo sticks. The tofu is then deep-fried until crispy and served piping hot. It can be enjoyed on its own or dipped in a variety of sauces, such as soy sauce, chili sauce, or a combination of sauces to balance the flavors.\\n\\nStinky tofu skewer | what to eat in nanjing\\nNanjing is dotted with street food stalls and night markets where you can find vendors cooking up and serving this pungent delicacy. Popular areas such as Fuzimiao (Confucius Temple) and Xinjiekou are particularly known for their stinky tofu offerings.\\n\\nStinky tofu street food stall | what to eat in nanjing\\nGansi Tofu\\nGansi tofu is another beloved tofu dish in Nanjing, appreciated for its simplicity, gentle flavors, and comforting qualities.\\n\\nGansi tofu | best food in nanjing\\nThe main components of Gansi tofu are tofu and a clear broth. The tofu used is typically a soft or silken variety that has a smooth and custard-like texture. The broth is made by simmering ingredients such as dried shiitake mushrooms, bamboo shoots, dried shrimp, or chicken bones to extract their flavors.\\n\\nSome ingredients of to cook Gansi | best food in nanjing\\nTo make Gansi tofu, the tofu is first cut into small cubes or slices. The broth is prepared separately by simmering the ingredients in water to create a fragrant and flavorful base. The tofu is then gently added to the broth to heat through without breaking apart. The broth provides a savory and aromatic base, while the tofu absorbs the flavors of the broth, adding a creamy and delicate taste to the dish. The combination of the two creates a comforting and satisfying experience.\\n\\nGansi broth with chicken | best food in nanjing\\nGansi tofu is typically served in a small bowl or individual soup bowls. The tofu cubes are immersed in the broth, and the dish is garnished with chopped green onions or cilantro for added freshness and visual appeal. It can be enjoyed on its own or served alongside other dishes as part of a larger meal. It pairs well with steamed rice, as the rice can be mixed with the broth to create a flavorful combination. Some people also enjoy adding soy sauce, vinegar, or chili oil to enhance the taste.\\n\\n| best food in nanjing\\nGansi tofu is commonly found in local eateries, traditional restaurants, and even street food stalls in Nanjing. You can enjoy this dish at Nanjing Impressions at No. 2, Shiziqiao, Gulou District for 3.5 USD per bowl.\\n\\nServing portions in small bowls | best food in nanjing\\nMandarin Sweet and Sour Fish\\nMandarin-style sweet and sour fish, also known as ‚ÄúTang Cu Yu‚Äù in Chinese, is a regional variation of the classic Chinese sweet and sour fish dish. It reflects the culinary style and flavor preferences of the Mandarin cuisine, which is prevalent in the northern regions of China, including Nanjing.\\n\\nMandarin-style sweet and sour fish | best food in nanjing\\nThe fish is typically marinated with salt, pepper, and sometimes Shaoxing wine or rice wine for added flavor. It is then coated with cornstarch or a batter made from a combination of flour and cornstarch and deep-fried until golden and crispy.¬†The sauce is prepared separately by combining vinegar, sugar, ketchup, soy sauce, and other seasonings in a wok or saucepan.\\n\\n| best food in nanjing\\nMandarin sweet and sour fish emphasizes a balance of sweet and sour flavors. The sauce has a tangy and slightly sweet taste, with a hint of saltiness from the soy sauce. Nanjing-style sweet and sour fish often leans towards a slightly sweeter profile compared to other regional variations. The crispy fried fish provides a delightful contrast to the sauce, offering a combination of textures.\\n\\nSweet and sour fish fillets | best food in nanjing\\nMandarin sweet and sour fish in Nanjing is typically served hot and garnished with sliced green onions or cilantro for freshness and visual appeal. It is often presented on a large plate or a serving platter, allowing the vibrant fish and sauce to be showcased. This dish is definitely suitable for a warm family meal. So, give it a try when you visit Nanjing!\\n\\nAnother presentation of sweet and sour fish | best food in nanjing\\nFreshwater Crabs\\nFreshwater crabs, also known as ‚ÄúNan Jing Da Zha Xie‚Äù in Chinese, refer to crabs that are harvested from the rivers, lakes, and fields around Nanjing. They are known for their delicate flavor, tender meat, and unique characteristics specific to the region.\\n\\n| best food in nanjing\\nFreshwater crabs are often prepared by steaming or boiling to preserve their natural flavors. Before cooking, the crabs are cleaned and seasoned. They are then cooked until their shells turn a vibrant orange-red color. The crabs are typically served whole, and the meat is enjoyed by cracking the shell and extracting it using specialized crab utensils.\\n\\nThere are various ways to enjoy freshwater crabs in Nanjing. Some popular dishes include steamed whole crabs, crab roe xiaolongbao (steamed soup dumplings), crab meat-filled dumplings, stir-fried crab with ginger and scallions, and crab meat fried rice. These dishes showcase the natural sweetness and unique characteristics of the crabs.\\n\\nWhere to try freshwater crabs in Nanjing?\\nGao You Seafood Street: Located in the Gaochun District of Nanjing, this street is lined with seafood restaurants specializing in freshwater field crab dishes. It‚Äôs a popular destination for locals and visitors alike.\\n\\nA street food stall offering crabs\\nNanjing Hexi Crab Market: This market is dedicated to freshwater field crabs and offers a vibrant atmosphere where you can select live crabs and have them prepared on-site at the market‚Äôs restaurants.\\nOf course, there are more options of food when it comes to Nanjing cuisine, but we hope those top specialties of the place will satisfy your food adventure on your next visit to Nanjing.\\n\\nSome best day tours, trips, activities and transfer services, tickets in, from and to Nanjing you can refer to\\n\\nPorcelain Tower of Nanjing\\nNanjing Presidential Palace Ticket\\nNanjing City Private Car Charter\\nDaming Mansion Zhanyuan Garden Ticket in Nanjing\\nChaotian Palace Ticket in Nanjing (For Mainland China ID Holders)\\nNanjing Zhouyuan Ticket\\nYufa Ecotourism Area Ticket in Nanjing\\nZiqinghu Hotspring Ticket in Nanjing\\nHongshan Forest Zoo Ticket in Nanjing (For Mainland Chinese Citizens Only)\\nMing Xiaoling Mausoleum Ticket\\n\\n\\nRead more China guide here and Nanjing guide here.\\nRelated articles\\n\\nTokyo itinerary 7 days ‚Äî How to spend 7 days in Tokyo & what to do in Tokyo for 7 days\\nZermatt travel blog ‚Äî The fullest Zermatt travel guide blog & the detailed Zermatt itinerary 2 days\\n5 best islands in Southeast Asia to discover in this summer\\n16+ photos show the beautiful of sunscapes in the Sea of Cortez, Mexico\\nKa Lam Retreat Ninh Van Bay ‚Äî The 5-star resort in Nha Trang, Vietnam\\nSinai blog ‚Äî The quick Sinai travel guide for a journey to the sacred land of Egypt\\n1 day in Melbourne ‚Äî How to spend 24 hours in Melbourne & Explore the best of Melbourne in a day perfectly?\\nSapporo itinerary ‚Äî How to spend 36 hours in Sapporo at the weekend?\\n\\n\\nNikki Dang\\nRELATED ARTICLESMORE FROM AUTHOR\\n\\nInspiration + Guide\\nWhat souvenirs to buy in Taiwan? This dish boasts a rich cultural heritage and tantalizes the taste buds with its unique blend of spices and tender meat. The preparation involves a meticulous salt-curing process that not only enhances the flavor but also preserves the duck, making it a popular choice during festive occasions and traditional banquets.\\nIn this article, you will learn how to make Nanjing Salted Duck at home, uncover its essential ingredients, and explore some variations that can elevate your dining experience. Whether you‚Äôre a seasoned chef or a novice cook, this guide will help you master the art of crafting this mouthwatering dish!\\nIngredients\\n| Ingredient | Measurement | Description |\\n| --- | --- | --- |\\n| Duck (whole) | 1 (about 4-5 lbs) | Opt for a fresh duck to achieve the best flavor and texture in your Nanjing Salted Duck. |\\n| Coarse salt | 1 cup | This is essential for the curing process that gives the duck its signature flavor. |\\n| Szechuan peppercorns | 1 tablespoon | Provides a unique, numbing spice that adds depth to the dish. |\\n| Star anise | 2 pods | This aromatic spice elevates the overall flavor profile, giving it a warm undertone. |\\n| Ginger | 4 slices | Fresh ginger enhances aroma and flavor, making the dish more aromatic. |\\n| Garlic | 4 cloves | Fresh garlic enhances the aroma and depth of flavor in Nanjing Salted Duck. |\\n| Green onions | 2 stalks | Used in the cooking process for added fragrance and taste. |\\n| Soy sauce | 1/4 cup | Adds a savory component that complements the saltiness of the dish. |\\nStep-by-Step Instructions\\n\\nPrepare the Duck: Rinse the duck thoroughly under cold water and pat it dry with paper towels. This ensures that the salt adheres well during the curing process.\\nSalt Cure: In a bowl, mix the coarse salt with Szechuan peppercorns, star anise, ginger, and crushed garlic. Rub this mixture generously all over the duck, including the cavity. Place the duck in a large dish, cover it with plastic wrap, and let it cure in the fridge for 24 hours.\\nRinse and Dry: After the curing time, remove the duck from the fridge. Rinse off the salt mixture under cold running water. Pat the duck dry once again. This step helps in balancing the flavors.\\nPrepare for Cooking: In a pot, bring water to a boil and add the green onions and soy sauce for extra flavor. Once boiling, carefully add the duck into the pot.\\nSimmer: Reduce the heat and let the duck simmer for about 1.5 hours. This slow cooking method ensures the meat becomes tender and absorbs all the aromatic flavors.\\nCool and Serve: Once cooked, remove the duck from the pot and let it cool slightly. Slice it into serving pieces and enjoy your homemade Nanjing Salted Duck with steamed rice or pickled vegetables.\\n\\nPro Tips\\n\\nUse Fresh Ingredients: Fresh herbs and spices can significantly enhance the flavor of your Nanjing Salted Duck.\\nAdjust Saltiness: If you prefer a less salty flavor, reduce the curing time to 12 hours.\\nExperiment with Marinades: Feel free to add your favorite spices or marinate the duck in soy sauce and wine for additional flavors.\\nServe with Condiments: Pairing this dish with a light sauce or fresh herbs can complement its rich flavors wonderfully.\\nReheat Gently: When reheating, do so gently to maintain the tenderness of the meat.\\n\\nNutritional Information\\n| Nutritional Component | Per Serving (100g) |\\n| --- | --- |\\n| Calories | 230 |\\n| Protein | 20g |\\n| Carbohydrates | 1g |\\n| Saturated Fats | 6g |\\n| Fiber | 0g |\\n| Cholesterol | 80mg |\\n| Sugars | 0g |\\n| Fat | 17g |\\nFAQs\\nWhat is the best way to store Nanjing Salted Duck?\\nTo store Nanjing Salted Duck, keep it wrapped tightly in plastic wrap or aluminum foil in the refrigerator for up to four days, or freeze it for longer storage.\\nCan Nanjing Salted Duck be made vegan or gluten-free?\\nWhile traditional Nanjing Salted Duck is not vegan, you could substitute duck with a firm tofu or seitan and use gluten-free soy sauce to create a similar flavor profile.\\nWhat are the best side dishes to serve with Nanjing Salted Duck?\\nSome popular side dishes include steamed rice, stir-fried vegetables, and pickled radishes, which balance the rich flavors of the duck.\\nHow long does it take to prepare Nanjing Salted Duck?\\nPreparation time is about 20 minutes, but remember to account for the 24 hours of curing time, plus 1.5 hours for cooking!\\nCan I freeze Nanjing Salted Duck for later?\\nYes, Nanjing Salted Duck freezes well. Just wrap it tightly in freezer-safe packaging for up to three months.\\nIs Nanjing Salted Duck spicy?\\nIt has a mild spice profile due to Szechuan peppercorns, providing a unique flavor without being too hot. Adjust the amount according to your preference!\\nCan I use other meats instead of duck?\\nWhile traditional recipes call for duck, you can experiment with chicken or even pork; however, cooking times may vary.\\nWhat‚Äôs the secret to achieving tender meat?\\nThe key lies in the slow simmering process, which allows the meat to absorb all the flavors while remaining tender.\\nNanjing Salted Duck isn‚Äôt just a dish; it‚Äôs a culinary experience that brings the flavors of Nanjing right to your home. ‚Äî 11+ best Nanjing street food & Nanjing famous food you must try\\nBy\\nNikki Dang\\n-\\nOctober 6, 2023\\n\\nNanjing, located in Jiangsu province, China, is a city with a rich history and cultural significance. It was the capital of several Chinese dynasties and served as the capital of the Republic of China in the early 20th century. Nanjing is known for its historical sites, beautiful landscapes, and, of course, its culinary specialties. So, what to eat in Nanjing? Let‚Äôs check out our suggested 11+ best food in Nanjing, Nanjing famous food and Nanjing street food you must try when coming to this beautiful ancient city!\\n\\nWhat to eat in Chengdu? ‚Äî 19+ must-try, famous food & best Chengdu street food to eat\\nWhat to eat in Shanghai? ‚Äî 17+ most popular, must eat & best street food in Shanghai\\nWhere to go in Shanghai at night? 25+ must-visit & best places to visit in Shanghai at night\\nWhat to do in Shanghai at night? 21+ top activities & best things to do in Shanghai at night\\n9+ most beautiful & best ancient towns in China\\n\\n \\nNanjing skyline\\n\\nA view of Nanjing Fuzimiao\\n\\nA busy street at Fuzimiao | nanjing street food\\n\\nNanjing street food | nanjing street food\\n\\n| nanjing street food\\nNanjing cuisine is one of the most influential and interesting features of China. Most visitors find the local delicacies here irresistible. Famous for its delicate preparation and rich flavors, each dish has its own charm. Now, let‚Äôs explore the best food of Nanjing and try it on your next visit to the ‚ÄúCapital of Six Dynasties‚Äù of China.\\n\\nNanjing typical food | nanjing street food\\nSalted Duck (top nanjing street food)\\nOne of Nanjing‚Äôs most beloved dishes is Nanjing salted duck. It is a traditional dish that has been enjoyed for centuries and holds a significant place in the local cuisine. It is a must-try specialty for food enthusiasts visiting the city, offering a unique and flavorful experience.\\n\\nNanjing salted duck | nanjing street food\\nThe preparation of Nanjing Salted Duck involves marinating the duck with a mixture of salt, spices, and other seasonings before air-drying or brining it. Nanjing salted duck has a unique flavor profile. The meat is savory, with a hint of sweetness and a delicate saltiness from the curing process. The skin is thin and crispy, offering a delightful contrast in texture to the tender meat.\\n\\nTexture of salted duck | nanjing street food\\nNanjing salted duck is typically served sliced, either as a standalone dish or as part of a larger meal. It is often accompanied by condiments like soy sauce, hoisin sauce, scallions, and cucumbers. The slices of salted duck can be wrapped in thin pancakes or enjoyed with steamed buns, allowing diners to create their own flavorful combinations.\\n\\nNanjing salted duck is typically served sliced | nanjing street food\\nWhere to try salted duck in Nanjing? (nanjing famous food)\\nWhen it comes to enjoying Nanjing salted duck, there are several popular addresses in Nanjing where you can savor this local delicacy. Here are a few renowned places:\\nNanjing Impressions: Hunan Walking Street, No.2 Shiziqiao Hunan Road. They serve authentic salted duck along with other local specialties in a nostalgic and culturally rich atmosphere.\\n\\nAt Nanjing Impressions | nanjing street food\\nLocal Street Food Stalls: In addition to restaurants, you can find street food stalls and local markets in Nanjing where vendors sell salted duck and other local delicacies. These stalls offer a more casual and authentic dining experience, allowing you to immerse yourself in the local food culture.\\n\\nA food stall selling salted ducks and roast ducks, @Visit Jiangsu FB | nanjing street food\\nJinling Roast Duck (what to eat in nanjing)\\nJinling roast duck is a famous variation of roast duck that originated in Nanjing. It is named after Nanjing‚Äôs historical moniker, ‚ÄúJinling,‚Äù which means ‚Äúcapital of Jin.‚Äù Although Jinling roast duck is not as famous around the world as Pecking roast duck in Beijing, its taste and scrumptiousness are just as exceptional.\\n\\nJinling roast duck | nanjing street food\\nSimilar to other roast duck dishes, Jinling roast duck involves a meticulous preparation process. The duck is first cleaned and dressed, and then it is marinated with a combination of various seasonings and spices. The marinade typically includes soy sauce, ginger, garlic, sugar, and other aromatic ingredients. The duck is left to absorb the flavors for a specific period, ensuring a rich and well-seasoned taste.\\n\\nRoasted in a closed oven | nanjing street food\\nAfter the preparation process, the duck is traditionally roasted in a closed oven using fruit tree wood as fuel. This roasting technique helps impart a distinctive smoky aroma and a beautiful golden-brown color to the duck. The slow and controlled roasting process ensures that the meat remains tender and succulent while the skin becomes crispy.\\n\\nJinling roast ducks ready on hooks | nanjing street food\\nWhen the roast duck is ready to serve, the meat is tender and juicy, infused with the aromatic blend of spices from the marinade. The skin is thin and crispy, providing a delightful contrast in texture. The combination of the savory meat and the flavorful skin creates a harmonious and satisfying taste.\\n\\nTender and juicy texture, @Maggie-Hiufu-Wong/CNN | nanjing street food\\nJinling roast duck is typically served sliced, accompanied by thin pancakes or steamed buns. The slices of duck are traditionally enjoyed by wrapping them in pancakes along with condiments like hoisin sauce, cucumber, scallions, and sometimes sugar or garlic paste.\\n\\nA good pair\\nWhere to try salted duck in Nanjing? (best food in nanjing)\\nNanjing Impressions: Hunan Walking Street, No.2 Shiziqiao Hunan Road, Nanjing.\\nNanjing Deji Plaza: 18 Zhongshan Rd, Xuanwu District, Nanjing. Deji Plaza is a popular shopping and dining complex in Nanjing. It houses several restaurants that serve Jinling roast duck, allowing you to savor this local specialty while exploring the vibrant city center.\\n\\nAnother way to enjoy Jinling roast duck is in thin slices | nanjing street food\\nFuzimiao (Confucius Temple) area and Shiziqiao Food Street, can also lead you to hidden gems and smaller establishments where you can indulge in authentic Jinling roast duck.\\n\\nShiziqiao Food Street | nanjing street food\\nDuck Blood Vermicelli Soup\\nDuck blood vermicelli soup, also known as ‚ÄúYa Xue Fen Si Tang‚Äù in Chinese, is a popular dish in Nanjing cuisine. The name of this dish sounds strange and you will surely be very curious, wondering how blood and soup are combined.\\n\\nDuck blood vermicelli soup | nanjing street food\\nThe soup is prepared by simmering the ingredients together in a flavorful broth. The duck blood curd is sliced and added to the soup, where it absorbs the flavors of the broth. The vermicelli noodles, duck meat, tofu, mushrooms, and other ingredients are also cooked in the broth until they are tender and infused with the soup‚Äôs flavors.\\n\\nA portion served in a small clay pot | nanjing street food\\nDuck blood vermicelli soup has a rich and savory flavor. The broth is usually seasoned with ingredients like soy sauce, ginger, garlic, and sometimes chili or other spices to add a touch of heat. The duck blood curd has a unique gelatinous texture and a mild, slightly metallic taste that blends well with the other ingredients in the soup.\\n\\nA flavorful bowl of duck blood vermicelli soup | nanjing street food\\nIt is typically served hot in a bowl and often garnished with chopped scallions or cilantro for added freshness and flavor.¬†You can find duck blood vermicelli soup easily in Nanjing, especially at food stalls in Fuzimiao food street for only 0.5 USD. You should try this delicious dish.\\nEgg Shaomai\\nEgg shaomai, also known as ‚ÄúDan Zi Shao Mai‚Äù in Chinese, is a popular street food and dim sum dish in Nanjing. It is primarily made with a combination of eggs, ground pork, shrimp, mushrooms, and other seasonings. The filling is typically mixed together and wrapped in a thin, delicate dumpling wrapper. It is a must-try when exploring the local food scene in Nanjing.\\n\\nEgg shaomai | nanjing famous food\\nThe preparation process for egg shaomai involves several steps. The filling ingredients are finely chopped or minced and mixed together with seasonings like soy sauce, ginger, garlic, and sometimes sesame oil or other spices. The mixture is then spooned onto a dumpling wrapper, folded into a pleated shape, and topped with a small piece of shrimp.\\nOnce assembled, the egg shaomai are traditionally steamed in bamboo steamers, allowing them to cook gently and retain their moisture. The steaming process ensures that the dumpling wrappers become soft and translucent while the filling is cooked to perfection.\\n\\nAnother look of egg shaomai | nanjing famous food\\nEgg shaomai has a delightful combination of flavors. The filling is savory and rich, with the umami taste of the pork and shrimp complemented by the earthiness of mushrooms and the aroma of seasonings. The addition of the egg provides a silky and creamy texture to the filling, enhancing its overall taste.\\n\\nEgg shaomai at Halal Ma Xiangxing restaurant | nanjing famous food\\nEgg shaomai is typically served in bamboo steamers, with each steamer holding several pieces of shaomai. It is often enjoyed as a snack or as part of a dim sum meal. The shaomai can be eaten on their own or dipped in condiments such as soy sauce, chili oil, or a combination of sauces for added flavor.\\nWonderful egg shaomai at Halal Ma Xiangxing restaurant is recommended ‚Äì where the dish was invented for a Chinese general who loved shaomai and shrimp. Here, they use fresh shrimp made into a paste and wrapped in a thin egg-based dumpling. Address: No.32, Yunnan North Road, Gulou District, Nanjing; open daily from 6:30 a.m. to 8:30 p.m.\\n\\n| nanjing famous food\\nTangbao (soup dumplings)\\nTangbao, also known as soup dumplings, is a type of dumpling filled with a flavorful broth and a mixture of meat and/or vegetables. They are known for their delicate and thin dumpling wrappers, which contain a hot, savory soup inside.\\n\\nTangbao (soup dumplings) | nanjing famous food\\nThe filling of Tangbao typically consists of minced pork, shrimp, crab meat, or a combination of these ingredients. Other variations may include vegetables such as bamboo shoots or mushrooms. The broth is made by simmering meat or bones, along with aromatic spices and seasonings, to create a flavorful and gelatinous soup.\\n\\nInviting tangbao | nanjing famous food\\nTangbao are traditionally steamed in bamboo steamers, which allows the dumplings to cook gently and retain their shape and juiciness. The steaming process activates the gelatin in the broth, transforming it into a hot, savory soup that is locked inside the dumpling.\\n\\nTangbao served in a bamboo steamer | nanjing street food\\nEnjoying Tangbao is a unique experience. The dumplings are typically served in bamboo steamers or small plates. To eat them, you can use chopsticks to carefully lift a Tangbao from the steamer, taking care not to puncture the delicate wrapper. You can then place the dumpling on a spoon and take a small bite from the corner to release the hot soup. Be cautious as the broth may be hot. You can then savor the combination of the flavorful soup and the filling. You will definitely fall in love with this adorable snack!\\n\\nWhat a delicious look! | nanjing famous food\\nTangbao are often served with a dipping sauce made from a combination of soy sauce, vinegar, and sometimes ginger or chili oil. This sauce adds an extra layer of tanginess and enhances the overall flavor of the dumplings.\\n\\nTangbao served with a dipping sauce | nanjing famous food\\nNanjing is known for its rich Tangbao culture, and there are numerous restaurants and street food stalls throughout the city that specialize in this dish. Some recommended places for you are:\\nYinshi Jishi Tangbao: No. 398 Mochou Road, Baixia District, Nanjing. They‚Äôre open every day from 6:30 a.m. to 7:30 p.m, and it costs about 1.8 USD for eight small bite-sized pieces of Tangbao.\\nFuzimiao (Confucius Temple) and Hunan Road are particularly renowned for their Tangbao offerings.\\nPan-fried Beef Dumplings\\nPan-fried beef dumplings, also known as ‚ÄúGuo Tie‚Äù or ‚ÄúJian Jiao‚Äù in Chinese, are a popular street food and snack in Nanjing. Pan-fried beef dumplings are a type of dumplings made with a thin wheat-based wrapper filled with a savory mixture of ground beef and seasonings. They are pan-fried until crispy on the bottom while maintaining a tender and juicy filling.\\n\\nPan-fried beef dumplings | nanjing famous food\\nThe filling for pan-fried beef dumplings typically consists of minced or ground beef combined with aromatics such as ginger, garlic, and green onions. Additional seasonings may include soy sauce, sesame oil, and sometimes spices like Sichuan peppercorns for a hint of heat.\\n\\nA tender and juicy filling | what to eat in nanjing\\nThe dumplings are cooked in a hot, oiled skillet or pan. They are first placed flat-side down and allowed to cook until the bottom becomes golden and crispy. Water is then added to the pan, and the dumplings are covered to steam. This steaming process helps to cook the filling thoroughly and ensure it remains juicy and tender. Once the water has evaporated, the dumplings continue to fry until the bottom becomes crispy again.\\n\\nThe dumplings are cooked in a hot, oiled skillet or pan. | what to eat in nanjing\\nPan-fried beef dumplings are typically served with a dipping sauce that adds an extra layer of flavor. Common dipping sauces include soy sauce, vinegar, and sometimes chili oil or sesame oil. Some people also enjoy adding minced garlic or ginger to the dipping sauce for additional zing.\\n\\n| what to eat in nanjing\\nWhere to try Pan-fried beef dumplings? (nanjing street food)\\nLiji Halal restaurant: No. 1, Dading Xiang, Pingshi Jie, Baixia District, Nanjing. The restaurant is open from 5:30 a.m. to 7:30 p.m. at a cost of around 0.7 USD for five pieces.\\n\\nLiji Halal Restaurant | what to eat in nanjing\\nPan-fried beef dumplings can also be found in various street food stalls, local eateries throughout Nanjing. They are often freshly made to order, ensuring their crispiness and deliciousness.\\nStinky Tofu\\nStinky tofu, also known as ‚ÄúChou Dou Fu‚Äù in Chinese, is a unique and polarizing street food in Nanjing. Whether you love stinky tofu or find it challenging, it is an intriguing culinary experience that represents the bold and diverse food culture of Nanjing.\\n\\nStinky tofu street food | what to eat in nanjing\\nThe process of making stinky tofu involves several steps. First, fresh tofu is soaked in brine made with various ingredients like fermented vegetables, dried shrimp, and spices. The tofu is then left to ferment for a period of time, from a few days to several weeks, depending on the desired intensity of flavor. After fermentation, the tofu is typically deep-fried until it develops a crispy golden exterior.\\n\\nStinky tofu cubes with crispy golden exterior | what to eat in nanjing\\nStinky tofu has a strong and pungent smell, which some describe as resembling rotten garbage or cheese. However, despite its odor, the taste of stinky tofu is often milder and more savory. The fermentation process gives the tofu a unique and complex flavor, with hints of umami and a slightly sour or tangy note.\\n\\n| what to eat in nanjing\\nStinky tofu is commonly served as a street food snack in Nanjing. It is often cut into bite-sized pieces and skewered on bamboo sticks. The tofu is then deep-fried until crispy and served piping hot. It can be enjoyed on its own or dipped in a variety of sauces, such as soy sauce, chili sauce, or a combination of sauces to balance the flavors.\\n\\nStinky tofu skewer | what to eat in nanjing\\nNanjing is dotted with street food stalls and night markets where you can find vendors cooking up and serving this pungent delicacy. Popular areas such as Fuzimiao (Confucius Temple) and Xinjiekou are particularly known for their stinky tofu offerings.\\n\\nStinky tofu street food stall | what to eat in nanjing\\nGansi Tofu\\nGansi tofu is another beloved tofu dish in Nanjing, appreciated for its simplicity, gentle flavors, and comforting qualities.\\n\\nGansi tofu | best food in nanjing\\nThe main components of Gansi tofu are tofu and a clear broth. The tofu used is typically a soft or silken variety that has a smooth and custard-like texture. The broth is made by simmering ingredients such as dried shiitake mushrooms, bamboo shoots, dried shrimp, or chicken bones to extract their flavors.\\n\\nSome ingredients of to cook Gansi | best food in nanjing\\nTo make Gansi tofu, the tofu is first cut into small cubes or slices. The broth is prepared separately by simmering the ingredients in water to create a fragrant and flavorful base. The tofu is then gently added to the broth to heat through without breaking apart. The broth provides a savory and aromatic base, while the tofu absorbs the flavors of the broth, adding a creamy and delicate taste to the dish. The combination of the two creates a comforting and satisfying experience.\\n\\nGansi broth with chicken | best food in nanjing\\nGansi tofu is typically served in a small bowl or individual soup bowls. The tofu cubes are immersed in the broth, and the dish is garnished with chopped green onions or cilantro for added freshness and visual appeal. It can be enjoyed on its own or served alongside other dishes as part of a larger meal. It pairs well with steamed rice, as the rice can be mixed with the broth to create a flavorful combination. Some people also enjoy adding soy sauce, vinegar, or chili oil to enhance the taste.\\n\\n| best food in nanjing\\nGansi tofu is commonly found in local eateries, traditional restaurants, and even street food stalls in Nanjing. You can enjoy this dish at Nanjing Impressions at No. 2, Shiziqiao, Gulou District for 3.5 USD per bowl.\\n\\nServing portions in small bowls | best food in nanjing\\nMandarin Sweet and Sour Fish\\nMandarin-style sweet and sour fish, also known as ‚ÄúTang Cu Yu‚Äù in Chinese, is a regional variation of the classic Chinese sweet and sour fish dish. It reflects the culinary style and flavor preferences of the Mandarin cuisine, which is prevalent in the northern regions of China, including Nanjing.\\n\\nMandarin-style sweet and sour fish | best food in nanjing\\nThe fish is typically marinated with salt, pepper, and sometimes Shaoxing wine or rice wine for added flavor. It is then coated with cornstarch or a batter made from a combination of flour and cornstarch and deep-fried until golden and crispy.¬†The sauce is prepared separately by combining vinegar, sugar, ketchup, soy sauce, and other seasonings in a wok or saucepan.\\n\\n| best food in nanjing\\nMandarin sweet and sour fish emphasizes a balance of sweet and sour flavors. The sauce has a tangy and slightly sweet taste, with a hint of saltiness from the soy sauce. Nanjing-style sweet and sour fish often leans towards a slightly sweeter profile compared to other regional variations. The crispy fried fish provides a delightful contrast to the sauce, offering a combination of textures.\\n\\nSweet and sour fish fillets | best food in nanjing\\nMandarin sweet and sour fish in Nanjing is typically served hot and garnished with sliced green onions or cilantro for freshness and visual appeal. It is often presented on a large plate or a serving platter, allowing the vibrant fish and sauce to be showcased. This dish is definitely suitable for a warm family meal. So, give it a try when you visit Nanjing!\\n\\nAnother presentation of sweet and sour fish | best food in nanjing\\nFreshwater Crabs\\nFreshwater crabs, also known as ‚ÄúNan Jing Da Zha Xie‚Äù in Chinese, refer to crabs that are harvested from the rivers, lakes, and fields around Nanjing. They are known for their delicate flavor, tender meat, and unique characteristics specific to the region.\\n\\n| best food in nanjing\\nFreshwater crabs are often prepared by steaming or boiling to preserve their natural flavors. Before cooking, the crabs are cleaned and seasoned. They are then cooked until their shells turn a vibrant orange-red color. The crabs are typically served whole, and the meat is enjoyed by cracking the shell and extracting it using specialized crab utensils.\\n\\nThere are various ways to enjoy freshwater crabs in Nanjing. Some popular dishes include steamed whole crabs, crab roe xiaolongbao (steamed soup dumplings), crab meat-filled dumplings, stir-fried crab with ginger and scallions, and crab meat fried rice. These dishes showcase the natural sweetness and unique characteristics of the crabs.\\n\\nWhere to try freshwater crabs in Nanjing?\\nGao You Seafood Street: Located in the Gaochun District of Nanjing, this street is lined with seafood restaurants specializing in freshwater field crab dishes. It‚Äôs a popular destination for locals and visitors alike.\\n\\nA street food stall offering crabs\\nNanjing Hexi Crab Market: This market is dedicated to freshwater field crabs and offers a vibrant atmosphere where you can select live crabs and have them prepared on-site at the market‚Äôs restaurants.\\nOf course, there are more options of food when it comes to Nanjing cuisine, but we hope those top specialties of the place will satisfy your food adventure on your next visit to Nanjing.\\n\\nSome best day tours, trips, activities and transfer services, tickets in, from and to Nanjing you can refer to\\n\\nPorcelain Tower of Nanjing\\nNanjing Presidential Palace Ticket\\nNanjing City Private Car Charter\\nDaming Mansion Zhanyuan Garden Ticket in Nanjing\\nChaotian Palace Ticket in Nanjing (For Mainland China ID Holders)\\nNanjing Zhouyuan Ticket\\nYufa Ecotourism Area Ticket in Nanjing\\nZiqinghu Hotspring Ticket in Nanjing\\nHongshan Forest Zoo Ticket in Nanjing (For Mainland Chinese Citizens Only)\\nMing Xiaoling Mausoleum Ticket\\n\\n\\nRead more China guide here and Nanjing guide here.\\nRelated articles\\n\\nTokyo itinerary 7 days ‚Äî How to spend 7 days in Tokyo & what to do in Tokyo for 7 days\\nZermatt travel blog ‚Äî The fullest Zermatt travel guide blog & the detailed Zermatt itinerary 2 days\\n5 best islands in Southeast Asia to discover in this summer\\n16+ photos show the beautiful of sunscapes in the Sea of Cortez, Mexico\\nKa Lam Retreat Ninh Van Bay ‚Äî The 5-star resort in Nha Trang, Vietnam\\nSinai blog ‚Äî The quick Sinai travel guide for a journey to the sacred land of Egypt\\n1 day in Melbourne ‚Äî How to spend 24 hours in Melbourne & Explore the best of Melbourne in a day perfectly?\\nSapporo itinerary ‚Äî How to spend 36 hours in Sapporo at the weekend?\\n\\n\\nNikki Dang\\nRELATED ARTICLESMORE FROM AUTHOR\\n\\nInspiration + Guide\\nWhat souvenirs to buy in Taiwan? Jinling Hotel paid off its capital construction debts of US$45¬†million in only 10 years.\", \"score\": 0.9183121, \"raw_content\": \"Contents\\n\\nJinling Hotel\\n\\n | This articleneeds additional citations forverification.Please helpimprove this articlebyadding citations to reliable sources. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.Find sources:\\\"Jinling Hotel\\\"‚Äìnews¬∑newspapers¬∑books¬∑scholar¬∑JSTOR(June 2019)(Learn how and when to remove this message)\\n\\n\\nJinling Hotel\\nJinling Hotel, Nanjing\\n\\nGeneral information\\nStatus | open\\nLocation | 2 Hanzhong Road\\nTown or city | Nanjing\\nCountry | People's Republic of China\\nOpened | March 1983\\nCost | 85$/night\\nOwner | Jinling Holdings Ltd\\nTechnical details\\nFloor count | 37\\nDesign and construction\\nArchitect(s) | P&T\\nOther information\\nNumber of rooms | 585\\nWebsite\\nhttp://www.jinlinghotel.com/English/index.aspx\\nJinling Hotel Nanjing (simplified Chinese: ÈáëÈôµÈ•≠Â∫ó; traditional Chinese: ÈáëÈôµÈ£ØÂ∫ó; pinyin: Jƒ´nl√≠ng F√†ndi√†n) is a hotel in Nanjing, China, located near the city's Xinjiekou district. \\\"Jinling\\\" is an old name for Nanjing which is often used to refer to the city in a poetic context. The hotel was Nanjing's first modern hotel managed by Chinese and is still often regarded as the pre-eminent five-star hotel in Nanjing.[citation needed] Jinling Hotel was the highest building in China until 1985, while Baiyun Hotel in Guangzhou built earlier was taller if including its antenna.[1]\\nThe hotel also has nine restaurants of differing cuisine types.[2] The Jinling Hotel Nanjing involves in many businesses such as chain fast food restaurants, travel agency services, car rental, communications, and advertising.\\n\\nJinling Hotel was designed by Palmer & Turner Group, P&T, an architectural firm in Hong Kong. P&T company designed Jinling Hotel's I, II, III phase building and Asia Pacific Tower.\\n\\nOverview\\n\\nLocation\\n\\nJinling Hotel is located on Hanzhong Road, Xinjiekou district, Jiangsu, China. Xinjiekou is located in the central of Nanjing and a famous commercial center with over 100 years of history. Jinling hotel is located on the northeastern part of Xinjiekou district.\\n\\nEnvironment and Social Responsibility\\n\\nJinling Hotel Nanjing Company vigorously carries out environmental protection activities and advocates green consumption and green living. The hotel also spent 16,000 square meters on lawns and ornamental tree planting.\\n\\nHistory\\n\\nIn 1978, Singaporean Chinese entrepreneur Tao Xinbo wants to build an international standard hotel in his hometown Nanjing catering oversea tourists. Under Tao Xinbo[3]'s effort, Jinling hotel become one of the six largest hotels catering foreign tourists approved by the State Council in 1979. In March 1979, Jinling hotel began its construction and Tao Xinbo invited architect James Kinoshita as designer. After 4 years construction, Jinling Hotel was successfully established on 21 February 1983, and located in the central business district of Nanjing. Jinling Hotel was also the first luxury five-start hotel in Jiangsu Province. Ever since open, JInling Hotel was popular and served hundreds of celebrities and politicians from different countries.\\n\\nIn 1983, the Jinling hotel was the tallest building in China at 110 meters and 37 floors tall. Jinling hotel has created many firsts. It has the first high-speed elevator in China, the first high-rise revolving restaurant in China, and China's first high-rise helipad. Ever since the Jinling hotel's establishment, many foreign media made lots of reports on the construction and opening of Jinling Hotel, including Canada, Britain, and Hong Kong. International media designate Jinling Hotel as the \\\"window of China's reform and opening up[4]\\\". At that time, Jinling Hotel was a mystery to Nanjing residents. The average price for a night was $90, and the only way for residents to know about Jinling Hotel was to buy tickets to visit the high-rise revolving restaurant, Xuan Gong. Jinling Hotel paid off its capital construction debts of US$45¬†million in only 10 years.\\n\\nIn May 1997, Jinling Hotel Phase II, the Nanjing World Trade Center was completed and started operation. The Nanjing World Trade Canter was 17 floors tall.\\n\\nIn October 2013, Jinling Hotel Phase III, the main building of Asia Pacific Tower was completed. Thus, Jinling Hotel Nanjing became the largest hotel complex in Jiangsu Province. The Asia Pacific Tower has a total of 53 floors and a height of 243 meters.\\n\\nAwards\\n\\nNotable events\\n\\nReferences\\n\\nExternal links\\n\\nvteCity ofNanjing\\nDistricts | Regional Variations\\nWhile Nanjing cuisine has its distinct identity, it also shares similarities with Jiangsu cuisine as a whole. Jiangsu cuisine is known for its emphasis on sweetness and careful preparation, which can also be seen in many Nanjing dishes.\\n5. Saltiness and Sweetness\\nDishes often balance salty and sweet flavors, with a preference for slightly sweet sauces. This is evident in many of their signature dishes.\\n6.
